A circle (omega) passes through (A) and is tangent to segment (overline{CD}) at point (T), with its center on line (BC). We need to compute (CT).1. :Answer:4 sqrt{5}-sqrt{7}Solution:Let A^{prime} be the reflection of A across B C, and let P=A B cap C D. Then since the center of omega lies on B C, we have that omega passes through A^{prime}. Thus, by power of a point, P T^{2}=P A cdot P A^{prime}. By similar triangles, we havefrac{P A}{A D}=frac{P B}{B C} Longrightarrow frac{P A}{2}=frac{P A+3}{8} Longrightarrow P A=1,and A^{prime} P=1+2 cdot 3=7, so P T=sqrt{7}. But by the Pythagorean Theorem, P C=sqrt{P B^{2}+B C^{2}}=4 sqrt{5}, and since T lies on segment C D, it lies between C and P, so C T=4 sqrt{5}-sqrt{7}.

:[<think>Okay, so I need to solve this inequality: -x + 2x + 3 > 0. Hmm, let me think. First, maybe I should rewrite the inequality to make it more familiar. Let (x = za) and (y = zb) where (gcd(a, b) = 1). Substituting these into the equation, we get:[za + (zb)^2 + z^3 = (za)(zb)z]Simplifying, we have:[za + z^2b^2 + z^3 = z^3ab]Dividing both sides by (z):[a + zb^2 + z^2 = z^2ab]Rearranging terms to solve for (a):[a = frac{z^2 + zb^2}{z^2b - 1}]We analyze possible values of (z) and solve for (a) and (b) ensuring (gcd(a, b) = 1). Case (z = 1):The equation simplifies to:[a + b^2 + 1 = ab]Solving for (a), we find:[a = frac{b^2 + 1}{b - 1}]Testing small values of (b), we find solutions:- (b = 2) gives (a = 5), so (x = 5), (y = 2)- (b = 3) gives (a = 5), so (x = 5), (y = 3) Case (z = 2):The equation simplifies to:[a + 2b^2 + 4 = 4ab]Solving for (a), we find:[a = frac{2b^2 + 4}{4b - 1}]Testing small values of (b), we find solutions:- (b = 1) gives (a = 2), so (x = 4), (y = 2)- (b = 3) gives (a = 2), so (x = 4), (y = 6) Higher values of (z) (3 and above) do not yield integer solutions for (a) and (b).Thus, the positive integer solutions are:[boxed{(4, 2)}, boxed{(4, 6)}, boxed{(5, 2)}, boxed{(5, 3)}],<think>Okay, so Tomi dropped a rubber ball from a certain height, right? :4. Let the height from which the ball is dropped to the ground be x. After the first bounce from the ground, the ball reached frac{3}{4} x of the initial height, just as much when dropped from that height. After the second bounce, the ball reached frac{3}{4}left(frac{3}{4} xright)=frac{9}{16} x of the initial height, just as much when dropped. After the third bounce and drop, the ball traveled a distance of frac{27}{64} x cdot 2. After the fourth bounce and drop, the ball traveled a distance of frac{81}{256} x cdot 2. Thus, the total distance traveled by the ball is x+2 xleft(frac{3}{4}+frac{9}{16}+frac{27}{64}+frac{81}{256}right)=653. We rearrange the equation to 653=frac{653}{128} x and solve for x=128 mathrm{~cm}.![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/2024_06_07_cd02ddf507985fa73630g-11.jpg?height=74&width=1642&top_left_y=2056&top_left_x=207)![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/2024_06_07_cd02ddf507985fa73630g-11.jpg?height=71&width=1636&top_left_y=2112&top_left_x=210)![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/2024_06_07_cd02ddf507985fa73630g-11.jpg?height=71&width=1636&top_left_y=2163&top_left_x=210)![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/2024_06_07_cd02ddf507985fa73630g-11.jpg?height=69&width=1636&top_left_y=2213&top_left_x=207)![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/2024_06_07_cd02ddf507985fa73630g-11.jpg?height=63&width=1636&top_left_y=2264&top_left_x=210)

:Three. (25 points) Let n be an integer. If there exist integers x, y, z satisfyingn=x^{3}+y^{3}+z^{3}-3 x y z text {, }then n is said to have property P.(1) Determine whether 1, 2, 3 have property P;(2) Among the 2014 consecutive integers 1, 2, cdots, 2014, how many do not have property P?

:[<think>Alright, let's tackle this problem step by step. The question is about something called "property P," which is defined for an integer n if there exist integers x, y, z such that n = x + y + z - 3xyz. There are two parts: first, determining whether 1, 2, and 3 have property P; second, figuring out how many numbers from 1 to 2014 do not have property P. Let's start with part (1).Part 1: Checking if 1, 2, 3 have property PFirst, I need to recall if there's a known identity or formula related to the expression x + y + z - 3xyz. Hmm... Oh, right! There's a factorization identity for this expression. Let me remember it.The formula is: x + y + z - 3xyz = (x + y + z)(x + y + z - xy - yz - zx). So this expression factors into the product of (x + y + z) and another quadratic expression. That seems useful.So, if n has property P, then n can be written as (x + y + z)(x + y + z - xy - yz - zx). Therefore, n must be divisible by (x + y + z) or the quadratic term. But since x, y, z are integers, both factors are integers. So, n must be expressible as a product of two integers in such a way.But maybe there's another way to approach this. I remember that x + y + z - 3xyz is also equal to (x + y + z) - 3(x + y + z)(xy + yz + zx) + 3xyz. Wait, no, maybe that's complicating things. Let's stick to the factorization.Given that n = (x + y + z)(x + y + z - xy - yz - zx), then possible values of n depend on the possible values of these two factors.But perhaps an even better approach is to consider specific cases where x + y + z = 0. Because if x + y + z = 0, then x + y + z = 3xyz. Therefore, in that case, n would be 0. But since n is supposed to be 1, 2, 3, maybe we need to look at cases where x + y + z is not zero.Alternatively, if x + y + z = k, then n can be written as k times (x + y + z - xy - yz - zx). So, n is a multiple of k. Therefore, for n to be 1, 2, or 3, which are small numbers, k must be a divisor of n. :(1) Let x=1, y=z=0, we get1=1^{3}+0^{3}+0^{3}-3 times 1 times 0 times 0 text {. }Thus, 1 has property P.Let x=y=1, z=0, we get2=1^{3}+1^{3}+0^{3}-3 times 1 times 1 times 0 text {. }Thus, 2 has property P.If 3 has property P, then there exist integers x, y, z such thatbegin{array}{l}3=(x+y+z)^{3}-3(x+y+z)(xy+yz+zx) Rightarrow 3left|(x+y+z)^{3} Rightarrow 3right|(x+y+z) Rightarrow 9 midleft[(x+y+z)^{3}-3(x+y+z)(xy+yz+zx)right] Rightarrow 9 mid 3,end{array}which is impossible.Therefore, 3 does not have property P.(2) Let f(x, y, z)=x^{3}+y^{3}+z^{3}-3xyz. :If the line a^{2}x+2y+1=0 is perpendicular to the line x-ay-2=0, then the value of a is ( )A: 2 or 0B: -2 or 0C: 2D: -2

:[<think>Okay, so I need to find the value of 'a' such that the two given lines are perpendicular to each other. The lines are ax + 2y + 1 = 0 and x - ay - 2 = 0. The answer choices are A: 2 or 0, B: -2 or 0, C: 2, D: -2. Hmm, let's start by recalling how to determine if two lines are perpendicular.First, I remember that if two lines are perpendicular, the product of their slopes is -1. So, I need to find the slopes of both lines and set their product equal to -1, then solve for 'a'. That sounds like a plan. Let me try that.Starting with the first line: ax + 2y + 1 = 0. However, in the options provided, the correct answer is A:2 or 0.Final Answerboxed{A}</think>To determine the value of (a) such that the lines (a^2x + 2y + 1 = 0) and (x - ay - 2 = 0) are perpendicular, we use the condition for perpendicularity of two lines in standard form (A_1A_2 + B_1B_2 = 0).1. For the first line (a^2x + 2y + 1 = 0), the coefficients are (A_1 = a^2) and (B_1 = 2).2. For the second line (x - ay - 2 = 0), the coefficients are (A_2 = 1) and (B_2 = -a).Applying the perpendicularity condition:[A_1A_2 + B_1B_2 = 0]Substituting the coefficients:[a^2 cdot 1 + 2 cdot (-a) = 0]Simplifying:[a^2 - 2a = 0]Factoring out (a):[a(a - 2) = 0]This gives the solutions:[a = 0 quad text{or} quad a = 2]To verify:- When (a = 0), the first line becomes (2y + 1 = 0) (a horizontal line), and the second line becomes (x - 2 = 0) (a vertical line), which are perpendicular.- When (a = 2), the slopes of the lines are (-2) and (frac{1}{2}), whose product is (-1), confirming perpendicularity.Thus, the values of (a) are (0) or (2), corresponding to option A.[boxed{A}]]

:Since the two lines are perpendicular to each other, we have a^{2}-2a=0. Therefore, a=2 or a=0.Hence, the correct choice is boxed{A}.
